                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">خلا</orth>
                  </form>, (S, Msb, K,) aor. <foreign lang="ar">يَخْلُو</foreign>, (S, Msb,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">خُلُوٌّ</foreign>, (S, Msb, K,) or <foreign lang="ar">خَلَآءٌ</foreign>, (Msb,) or both, (K,) said of a place, (K,) of a place of alighting or abode, (Msb,) and of a thing, (S, TA,) <hi rend="ital">It was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, empty, vacant, void, devoid, destitute,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">unoccupied;</hi> (K, TA;) <hi rend="ital">had none,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">nothing, in it;</hi> (TA;) as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n11418-1" target="اخلى" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, (Msb, K,) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n11418-2" target="استخلى" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, (K.) [<foreign lang="ar">خَلَا المَكَانُ مِنَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">النَّاسُ وَ المَآءِ وَالكَلَأ</foreign> means <hi rend="ital">The place was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, devoid,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">destitute, of human beings and water and herbage or pasturage; without human beings</hi> &amp;c.] Of a place of alighting or abode, you say, <foreign lang="ar">خَلَا مِنْ أَهْلِهِ</foreign> and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n11418-3" target="اخلى" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> [<hi rend="ital">It was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, devoid,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">destitute, of its occupants</hi>]. (Msb.) And of a vessel, <foreign lang="ar">خَلَا مِمَّا فِيهِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">It was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, empty of what was in it.</hi> (Mgh.) And <foreign lang="ar">خَلَوْتُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عَنِ الطَّعَامِ</foreign> (S) <hi rend="ital">I became empty, in the belly, of food;</hi> (PS;) and <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n11418-4" target="أَخْلَيْتُ" n="4" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>عَنْهُ</foreign> signifies the same. (S.) And <foreign lang="ar">خَلَا مِن العَيْبِ</foreign>, (Msb,) or <foreign lang="ar">عَنِ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الأَمْرِ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">مِنْهُ</foreign>, (Kudot;,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">خُلُوٌّ</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">He was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, free</hi> (Msb, K) <hi rend="ital">from fault,</hi> (Msb,) or <hi rend="ital">from the thing,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">affair:</hi> (K:) and, accord. to IAar, <foreign lang="ar">خلا</foreign> alone signifies <hi rend="ital">he was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, free from a fault,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">the like, of which he was accused,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">suspected.</hi> (TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">خَلَتْ عَنْ مَانِعِ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">النِّكَاحِ</foreign>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">خُلُوٌّ</foreign>, is said of a woman [as meaning <hi rend="ital">She was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, free from any obstacle to marriage</hi>]. (Msb.) Accord. to the K, <foreign lang="ar">خَلَا مَكَانُهُ</foreign> [lit. <hi rend="ital">His place became vacant</hi>] means <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">he died:</hi> but accord. to IAar, <foreign lang="ar">خَلَا</foreign> alone has this signification [from the same verb signifying <foreign lang="ar">مَضَى</foreign>. explained below]: and if you add <foreign lang="ar">مكانه</foreign>, you say <foreign lang="ar">خَلَّى</foreign>, with teshdeed; which see below. (TA.) You say also, <foreign lang="ar">خَلَا لَكَ الشَّىْءُ</foreign> and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n11418-5" target="اخلى" n="5" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, both signifying the same, (AA, S, TA,) <hi rend="ital">i. q.</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">فَرَغَ</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">The thing was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, vacant,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">unoccupied, for thee:</hi> (see an ex. of the former verb in a saying of Tarafeh cited voce <foreign lang="ar">جَوٌّ</foreign>:) and hence, <hi rend="ital">the thing was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, exclusively for thee</hi>]. (TA.) AA cites as an ex. the saying of Maan Ibn-Ows, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">أَعَاذِلُ هَلْ يَأْتِى القَبَائِلَ حَظُّهَا</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L><foreign lang="ar">مِنَ المَوْتِ أَمْ <ref cref="n11418-6" target="أَخْلَى" n="6" type="5" subtype="TFSO" lang="ar"/>لَنا المَوْتُ وَحْدَنَا</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">O censurer, does their share of death come to the tribes</hi> in common, <hi rend="ital">or is death exclusively for us alone?</hi>]. (S, TA.) See also the paragraph, below, commencing with <foreign lang="ar">خَلَا</foreign> as a word denoting exception.          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  [Hence,] <foreign lang="ar">خَلَا</foreign> and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n11418-7" target="اخلى" n="7" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, (S, K,) said of a man, (TA,) or the same two verbs followed by <foreign lang="ar">بِنَفْسِهِ</foreign>, said of a man, (Msb,) both signify the same; (S;) <hi rend="ital">He was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became,</hi> [<hi rend="ital">without any companion,</hi> i. e.] <hi rend="ital">alone, by himself;</hi> (Msb;) or <hi rend="ital">he became</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">وَقَعَ</foreign> [q. v.]) <hi rend="ital">in a vacant place, in which he was not pressed against,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">straitened.</hi> (K.) And <foreign lang="ar">خَلَا بِهِ</foreign>, (S, Msb, K,) and <foreign lang="ar">إِلَيْهِ</foreign>, (S, K,) and <foreign lang="ar">مَعَهُ</foreign>, (K,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">خَلْوَةٌ</foreign> (S, Msb, K) and <foreign lang="ar">خَلَآءٌ</foreign> (S, K) and <foreign lang="ar">خَلْوٌ</foreign>, (K, TA,) or <foreign lang="ar">خُلُوٌّ</foreign>, (CK,) or the first of these, i. e. <foreign lang="ar">خَلْوَةٌ</foreign>, is a simple subst., and the second and third are the inf. ns.; (TA;) and <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n11418-8" target="اخلى" n="8" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>به</foreign>, (Lh, K,) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n11418-9" target="اخلاهُ" n="9" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, (S, K,) and <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n11418-10" target="استخلى" n="10" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>بِهِ</foreign>; (K; [the last omitted in the CK;]) <hi rend="ital">He was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, alone with him;</hi> (Msb;) <hi rend="ital">he was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, in company with him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">he met him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">had a meeting or an interview with him, in a vacant place,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">a place unoccupied</hi> [<hi rend="ital">by others,</hi> i. e., <hi rend="ital">in a private place</hi>]. (S, K.) In the saying in the Kur [ii. 13], <foreign lang="ar">وَإِذَا خَلَوْا إِلَى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">شَيَاطِينِهِمْ</foreign>, it is said that <foreign lang="ar">إِلَى</foreign> is used in the sense of <foreign lang="ar">مَعَ</foreign>, [so that the meaning is <hi rend="ital">And when they are alone with their devils,</hi>] as in that other saying in the Kur [iii. 45 and lxi. 14], <foreign lang="ar">مَنْ أَنْصَارِى إِلَى ٱللّٰهُ</foreign>. (S.) A man says to another man, <foreign lang="ar">اُخْلُ مَعِى حَتَّى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">أُكَلِّمَكَ</foreign>, i. e. <hi rend="ital">Be</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">come</hi>] <hi rend="ital">thou alone with me</hi> [<hi rend="ital">that I may speak to thee</hi> in private]. (TA.) And one says, <foreign lang="ar">خَلَا بِزَوْجَتِهِ</foreign>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">خَلْوَةٌ</foreign>, [but see what is said of this noun above,] <hi rend="ital">He was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, alone with his wife:</hi> but [properly speaking, according to the law,] the term <foreign lang="ar">خَلْوَةٌ</foreign> [or <foreign lang="ar">خَلْوَةٌ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">صَحِيحَةٌ</foreign>, in this case,] is not used unless it be <hi rend="ital">with the enjoyment of</hi>

                  </form> as a word denoting exception, (S, Mughnee, K,) when it governs a gen. case, (S, Mughnee,) as when you say, <foreign lang="ar">جَاؤُونِى خَلَا زَيْدٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">They came to me, except Zeyd</hi>], is a particle, (S, Mughnee, K,) accord. to some of the grammarians, like <foreign lang="ar">حَاشَى</foreign>; but accord. to some, a prefixed inf. n. (S.) ↓ It. also governs an accus. case, as a verb: (S, Mughnee:) so that you say, <foreign lang="ar">جَاؤُونِى خَلَا زَيْدًا</foreign> [meaning as above]; the agent of <foreign lang="ar">خلا</foreign> being implied, (S, Mughnee, *) like that of <foreign lang="ar">حَاشَى</foreign> [used as a verb]: it is as though you said, <foreign lang="ar">خَلَا مَنْ جَآءَنِى مِنْ زَيْدٍ</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">those who came to me were without Zeyd</hi>]: (S:) or correctly, accord. to IB, <foreign lang="ar">خَلَا بَعْضُهُمْ زَيْدًا</foreign> [for <foreign lang="ar">مِنْ زَيْدٍ</foreign>, like as you say, <foreign lang="ar">خَلَاكَ ذَمٌّ</foreign>, for <foreign lang="ar">خَلَا</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عَنْكَ ذَمٌّ</foreign>]. (TA.)                   <foreign lang="ar">شَجِىٌّ</foreign>. (S.) It is said in a prov., <foreign lang="ar">لِلشَّجِىِّ مِنَ <ref cref="n11429-21" target="الخَلِىِّ" n="21" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>وَيْلٌ</foreign>, i. e. <hi rend="ital">Woe to him who is occupied by anxiety from him who is free therefrom:</hi> (TA:) and in another, <foreign lang="ar">مِنَ <ref cref="n11429-22" target="الخَلِىِّ" n="22" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>مَا يَلْقَى الشَّجِىُّ</foreign>, i. e. <hi rend="ital">What will he who is occupied by anxiety experience from him who is free therefrom?</hi> meaning, accord. to AO, that the latter will not aid the former against his anxieties, but will censure him: it is said in the Tekmileh that <foreign lang="ar">الخَلِىّ</foreign> [in these provs.] is from <foreign lang="ar">خَلَاهُ الحُزْنُ</foreign> meaning “ Grief passed away from him, ” and “ quitted him. ” (Har p. 590.) And   
      <foreign lang="ar">أَنْتِ <ref cref="n11429-23" target="خَلِيَّةٌ" n="23" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n11427"/></foreign> means <foreign lang="ar">خَالِيَةٌ مِنَ الخَيْرِ</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">Thou,</hi> O woman, <hi rend="ital">art devoid,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">destitute, of good</hi>]. (Mgh.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  Also A man <hi rend="ital">having no wife;</hi> (S, K;) [for <foreign lang="ar">خَالٍ مِنَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الزَّوَجَاتِ</foreign>, a phrase occurring in the TA:] and a woman <hi rend="ital">having no husband;</hi> (K;) thus without <foreign lang="ar">ة</foreign>: (TA:) pl. <foreign lang="ar">أَخْلَآءٌ</foreign>: (K:) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n11429-24" target="خِلْوَةٌ" n="24" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, also, has the latter meaning; dual <foreign lang="ar">خِلْوَتَانِ</foreign>, and pl. <foreign lang="ar">خِلْوَاتٌ</foreign>: and so has   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n11429-25" target="مُخْلِيَةٌ" n="25" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>: and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n11429-26" target="خَلِيَّةٌ" n="26" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n11427"/></foreign> means a woman <hi rend="ital">having no husband nor children;</hi> pl. <foreign lang="ar">خَلِيَّاتٌ</foreign>. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  [And <hi rend="ital">Alone;</hi> as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n11429-27" target="مُخْلٍ" n="27" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n11430"/></foreign>, and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n11429-28" target="خِلْوٌ" n="28" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n11423"/></foreign>.] It is said in a prov., <foreign lang="ar">الذِّئْبُ <ref cref="n11429-29" target="مُخْلِيًا" n="29" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>أَشَدُّ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The wolf when</hi> [<hi rend="ital">alone</hi> or] <hi rend="ital">in a vacant place</hi> [<hi rend="ital">is most courageous,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">violent</hi>]; (TA;) or <foreign lang="ar">خَالِيًا</foreign> [which means the same]. (JK. [And another reading is <foreign lang="ar">أَسَدٌ</foreign>. See Freytag's Arab. Prov., i. 500.]) And one says,   
      <foreign lang="ar">وَجَدْتُ فُلَانَةَ <ref cref="n11429-30" target="مُخْلِيَةً" n="30" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, meaning <foreign lang="ar">خَالِيَةً</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">I found such a woman alone</hi>]. (TA.) And   
      <foreign lang="ar">وَجَدَهُمَا <ref cref="n11429-31" target="خِلْوَيْنِ" n="31" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> i. e. <foreign lang="ar">خَالِيَيْنِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He found them two alone</hi>]. (K.)          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  [Also <hi rend="ital">Past,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">past away</hi>: as well as <hi rend="ital">going, going away,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">passing away.</hi>] <foreign lang="ar">القُرُونُ خَالِيَةُ</foreign> means [<hi rend="ital">The generations</hi>] <hi rend="ital">that have passed.</hi> (JK, S, TA.)
